601 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


In re Metropolitan Baptist Church of Richmond, Inc.


Civ. No. 34194


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


48 Cal. App. 3d 850; 121 Cal. Rptr. 899; 1975 Cal. App. LEXIS 1162



June 4, 1975 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Contra Costa County, No. R-21914, Martin E. Rothenberg, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed, and the motion to dismiss the appeal is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant church sought review of the Superior Court of Contra Costa County (California), which entered a judgment distributing its assets upon dissolution as required by Cal. Corp. Code § 9801. Respondent attorney general was joined as required by statute. Appellant contended that the trial court invaded its U.S. Const. amend. I rights and misapplied the cy pres doctrine.


OVERVIEW: Appellant church voted to disband and distribute its assets to other congregations after its membership declined precipitously. Appellant petitioned the trial court for authority to distribute its assets in accordance with the vote of its membership pursuant to Cal. Corp. Code § 9801. Respondent attorney general was joined in the proceedings as directed by statute. The trial court altered the plan for distribution submitted by appellant. Appellant claimed that the trial court invaded its U.S. Const. amend. I rights and misapplied the cy pres doctrine. The court disagreed and affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court held that ecclesiastical concerns were incidental and remote because this case dealt with the disposition of church property, and therefore the establishment clause of U.S. Const. amend. I was not offended. The court held that the cy pres doctrine was correctly applied because the assets of appellant were divided between two churches of similar fundamentalist persuasion which were nearest geographically to appellant's town thus preserving the intent of appellant's benefactors.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's plan to distribute the assets of appellant church. Respondent attorney general was joined as required by statute. The court held that the establishment clause of U.S. Const. amend. I was not offended because this was a property dispute and found that the trial court correctly applied the cy pres doctrine to effect the intent of appellant's benefactors.

 

602 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Ernst


Crim. No. 25477


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Five


48 Cal. App. 3d 785; 121 Cal. Rptr. 857; 1975 Cal. App. LEXIS 1154



June 3, 1975 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The Petition of Respondent Williams for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied July 30, 1975.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. A-606968, Carlos E. Velarde, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The order is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The People challenged an order from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) that granted defendants' motions to set aside the information charging them with a violation of Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11355.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were charged by information with a violation of Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11355 for agreeing to sell a narcotic and then delivering a non-narcotic substance. After they were held to answer, the superior court granted their motions to set aside the information. The People appealed. The police informant seized a substance from one defendant that was not cocaine or any other controlled substance although defendants promised cocaine. It was a crime to agree to sell a narcotic and then to deliver instead a non-narcotic substance. The trial court set aside the information because there was no delivery and, therefore, a necessary element of § 11355 was missing. The offense defined by § 11355 consisted of two elements: first, a "deal" to supply a controlled substance, and, second, some activity with respect to any other liquid, substance, or material in apparent consummation. The order was reversed and remanded for further proceedings because defendants delivered a non-narcotic substance in violation of the law.


OUTCOME: The order dismissing the informations against defendants was reversed because defendants could still be charged with delivering narcotics although the substance that they actually delivered was a non-narcotic substance.

 

603 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Carbonie


Crim. No. 25868


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


48 Cal. App. 3d 679; 121 Cal. Rptr. 831; 1975 Cal. App. LEXIS 1147



May 30, 1975 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied June 17, 1975, and Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied July 23, 1975.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. A-435078, Julius A. Leetham, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which convicted appellant, on a jury verdict, for three counts of using a minor as an agent to furnish controlled substances in violation of Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11380.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of three counts of using a minor as an agent to furnish controlled substances in violation of Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11380. Appellant sought the court's review, asserting various points of error, including that the five-year minimum prison term provided for her offense constituted cruel and unusual punishment in violation of Cal. Const. art. I, § 17. The court held that in examining whether a particular punishment was so disproportionate to the offense such that it constituted cruel and unusual punishment, three factors were considered. Those factors were the nature of the offense and/or the offender, the penalties imposed in the state for more serious crimes, and the penalties imposed by other states for the same offense. Here, the legislature determined that a violation of § 11380 was morally reprehensible and serious enough to merit a severe and certain penalty. Further, because § 11380 was designed to protect children, great deference was given to the legislature's judgment. Additionally, examinations of penalties imposed in the state and elsewhere did not indicate appellant was being cruelly or unusually punished. Judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Judgment of conviction was affirmed where the minimum mandatory sentence imposed upon appellant did not, in light of the seriousness of the crime for which she was convicted, constitute cruel and unusual punishment, and where a tape recording of a telephone conversation between appellant's son and a law enforcement officer was properly admitted into evidence.

 

604 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Stanley v. City and County of San Francisco


Civ. No. 33611


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Two


48 Cal. App. 3d 575; 121 Cal. Rptr. 842; 1975 Cal. App. LEXIS 1137



May 29, 1975 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco, No. 651896, Ira A. Brown, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment (order granting summary judgment) is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant individuals were injured in a motor vehicle accident and sought review of the order of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), which granted respondent city summary judgment under Cal. Gov't. Code § 945.6(a)(1) because appellants' claim was filed more than six months after rejection of their claims by respondent.


OVERVIEW: Appellant individuals were involved in a motor vehicle accident with a city police vehicle belonging to respondent city and filed timely claims pursuant to Cal. Gov't Code §§ 905 and 911.2, which were rejected. Appellants then filed their complaint for damages more than six months later and respondents obtained summary judgment under Cal. Gov't. Code § 945.6(a)(1). Appellants contended that the statutory requirements violated due process and equal protection. The court affirmed and held that the statutory provisions that defined with precision and clarity the respective rights and duties of both the individual claimants and the public entities were not unreasonable, arbitrary, or vague, and thus not subject to constitutional attack on due process grounds. The court further held that the statutory discrimination would not be set aside as a denial of equal protection of the laws if any state of facts reasonably could be conceived to justify it, and there were a number of reasons for the classification including affording the public entity the chance to correct the conditions or practices that gave rise to the claim.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed and held that the shortened filing requirements of the statute as applied to a public entity were constitutional because they were not unreasonable, arbitrary, or vague, and no equal protection violation existed because they were rationally related to a legitimate governmental interest.

 

605 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Contreras v. America, Compania General De Seguros, S.A.


Civ. No. 33495


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


48 Cal. App. 3d 270; 121 Cal. Rptr. 694; 1975 Cal. App. LEXIS 1112



May 16, 1975 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied June 13, 1975, and Respondent's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied July 9, 1975.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of San Mateo County, No. 168656, Frank W. Rose, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed with directions to the trial court to enter a summary judgment in favor of plaintiff pursuant to Code of Civil Procedure section 437c determining that America's policy affords insurance coverage to plaintiff and the minor children, that the applicable limits of liability are those prescribed in Vehicle Code section 16056 (former § 16059), and the cause of action is remanded to the superior court with directions to permit plaintiff to proceed with his cause of action for negligence and that of the minor children. Plaintiff shall recover his costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff insured appealed a judgment from the Superior Court of San Mateo County (California) in favor of defendant insurer, finding that an occupant-exclusion clause in plaintiff's automobile policy was valid.


OVERVIEW: In an action seeking to establish the limits of insurance protection under a policy of insurance issued in California by defendant insurance company, solely for liability arising out of the operation of a motor vehicle in Mexico, plaintiff appealed from a summary judgment in favor of defendant. The judgment adjudicated that the occupant-exclusion clause in the policy was valid, and that the liability limits were those provided for in the policy. On appeal, the court noted that, in view of public policy and the provisions of Cal. Ins. Code § 11580.1, a clause excluding coverage to the occupants of a motor vehicle was impermissible and invalid. The court concluded that the provisions of Cal. Ins. Code § 11580.1 were a part of the insurance contract, and that, under the statute, the occupant-exclusion clause was invalid. Pursuant to the statute's provisions, the liability limits were those therein provided, rather than the lesser limits provided for in the policy. The judgment was therefore reversed.


OUTCOME: The judgment for defendant insurer was reversed, with directions to the trial court to enter summary judgment in favor of plaintiff, because the automobile insurance policy at issue afforded coverage to plaintiff and minor children involved in the underlying automobile accident, where occupant-exclusion clause in policy was invalid as against public policy.

 

606 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Superior Court (Brodie)


Civ. No. 45299, Crim. No. 26411


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Four


48 Cal. App. 3d 195; 121 Cal. Rptr. 732; 1975 Cal. App. LEXIS 1105



May 14, 1975 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The Petitions of Real Party in Brodie and Appellant People for a Hearing by the Supreme Court were Denied July 30, 1975. Tobriner, J., was of the Opinion that the Petition of Real Party in Interest should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. A 186883, Burch Donahue, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Let a writ of mandate issue requiring the superior court to set aside that portion of its order of October 4, 1974, which struck an allegation of special circumstance from the information. The appeal (2d Crim. No. 26411) is dismissed as moot.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The prosecution appealed a decision from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which granted defendant's motion to strike the allegation pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 190.2(b)(4) of a prior murder conviction as a "special circumstance."


OVERVIEW: The prosecution charged defendant with two murders pursuant to separate counts that each alleged, as a special circumstance under Cal. Penal Code § 190.2(b)(4), the murder of the other victim as well as a murder conviction in a prior proceeding. The trial court granted defendant's motion to strike the prior conviction allegation, reasoning that when § 190.2(b)(4) authorized the death penalty if the defendant had "in this or in any prior proceeding been convicted of more than one offense of murder," the statute required conviction of more than one murder offense within a single prior proceeding before the prior conviction could constitute a special circumstance. After determining that the prosecution's petition for writ of mandate was an appropriate vehicle for interlocutory challenge to the trial court's decision, the court reversed, refusing to impute to the legislature an intent to create a statutory scheme that precluded charging special circumstances for multiple prior murder convictions unless those convictions were all obtained in a single trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court to strike the special circumstances charge because the court refused to interpret the relevant statute as evidencing a legislative intent to restrict the "multiple murder" special circumstance to situations in which the additional murder convictions had all been obtained in a single criminal proceeding.

 

607 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Bill Loeper Ford v. Hites


Civ. No. 44387


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Five


47 Cal. App. 3d 828; 121 Cal. Rptr. 131; 1975 Cal. App. LEXIS 1070



April 30, 1975 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. C57520, Norman R. Dowds, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff car dealer challenged the decision of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which dismissed its action for indemnity against defendant driver who purchased a car from the dealer and was subsequently involved in a car accident.


OVERVIEW: The car dealer sold a car to the driver, who then was involved in an accident with the car. The driver's passengers sued the dealer, among others, and the dealer settled with them. Subsequently, the dealer filed a complaint against the driver for indemnity, alleging that, by virtue of the settlement the dealer had entered into, the driver was obligated to indemnify the dealer for the amounts it was obligated to pay the plaintiffs in the prior lawsuits. The complaint also alleged that the sole basis of that recovery had been based on the car's design defect and that the dealer's liability was passive or secondary in nature. It also alleged that the driver had been negligent, attempting to shift liability to the driver. The court affirmed the trial court's dismissal of the action. Although the dealer was seeking reimbursement from the driver on the basis of the doctrine of implied indemnity, the court held that a retailer is strictly liable, regardless of fault, and that to allow indemnification because the driver was actively negligent in driving the automobile was the antithesis of strict liability.


OUTCOME: The trial court's dismissal was affirmed.

 

608 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Allums


Crim. No. 12943


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Two


47 Cal. App. 3d 654; 121 Cal. Rptr. 62; 1975 Cal. App. LEXIS 1055



April 29, 1975 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A petition for a rehearing was denied May 30, 1975, and appellant's petition for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied June 26, 1975.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Alameda County, No. 55791, Alan A. Lindsay, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The statements in the judgment and in the abstract of judgment "that the defendant was armed with a deadly weapon and did use a firearm" and that "the provisions of section 12022.5 of the Penal Code shall apply as to the use clause" are stricken, and the following is inserted in their place: "Defendant used a firearm in the commission of the offense within the meaning of Penal Code sections 1203 and 12022.5 but Penal Code sections 12022 and 3024 are not applicable." Otherwise, the judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of Alameda County (California), which convicted him of assaulting a police officer with a deadly weapon, in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 245(b).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of a violation of Cal. Penal Code § 245(b) for assaulting a police officer with his own gun. On appeal, the court modified the judgment, striking the finding that defendant was armed, and affirmed. The court held that evidence of defendant's prior conviction was admissible because it had a "clearly perceived" connection to the charged offense. The court held that defendant was not entitled to instructions on unconsciousness or the lesser-included offense of assault with a deadly weapon, Cal. Penal Code § 245(a), because the evidence did not justify such instructions. The court found that defendant did not meet his burden of showing a systematic use of peremptory challenges to exclude blacks over a period of time. The court held that defendant's sentence was correct under the present state of law.


OUTCOME: The court modified the judgment and affirmed defendant's conviction as modified. The court held that evidence of defendant's prior conviction was admissible, defendant was not entitled to instructions on unconsciousness or a lesser-included offense, and defendant did not show discrimination in the state's use of peremptory challenges.

Manalis Finance Co. v. Gedulig


Civ. No. 44667


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


47 Cal. App. 3d 672; 121 Cal. Rptr. 93; 1975 Cal. App. LEXIS 1057



April 29, 1975 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A petition for a rehearing was denied May 28, 1975, and appellant's petition for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied July 16, 1975.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. C75615, Robert A. Wenke, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant finance company sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) denying the enforceability of a lien assigned to appellant by a hospital against respondent State of California Department of Employment Development pursuant to Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 14115.5.


OVERVIEW: Appellant finance company was assigned an interest as a third party in state health fund payments due from a hospital. When appellant tried to enforce its interest against the hospital, it was denied because of a perfected tax lien filed against the hospital by defendant State of California Department of Economic Development. Appellant filed a claim with defendant, which was denied. The trial court also denied the claim. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 14115.5 rendered the assignment to appellant unenforceable because it could not defeat the levy of taxes imposed on the hospital by defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the ruling of the lower court, noting that any money due under the state health fund was subject to existing claims made under state or federal statutes.

 

610 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Gordon


Crim. No. 24383


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


47 Cal. App. 3d 465; 120 Cal. Rptr. 840; 1975 Cal. App. LEXIS 1038



April 24, 1975 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's petition for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied July 3, 1975.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. A295096, Albert D. Matthews, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant attorney appealed a conviction from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) for violation of Cal. Penal Code § 653f for solicitation of a bribe and from an order that denied her motion, pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 995, to quash the indictment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant attorney asked a police officer to plant narcotics on a third party and then arrest that party, for which defendant agreed to pay the police officer money. Defendant did not follow through with the scheme. Defendant was convicted of solicitation of a bribe, and she appealed. The court affirmed defendant's conviction for solicitation of a bribe under Cal. Penal Code § 653f as solicitation of a bribe could be stated in any form that carried the import of a bribe which was intended to be so understood. Also, defendant had the requisite intent to solicit when she asked the officer to accept a bribe and use his official capacity as a police officer to effect an arrest. The requirement in § 653f that there be corroborating evidence of the officer's testimony was satisfied by the testimony of another attorney from whom defendant obtained the police officer's name and a tape recording of defendant's soliciting the police officer. Moreover, defendant later withdrawing or failing to consummate the crime was not a defense to the charge. Finally, the denial of defendant's motion to quash the indictment under Cal. Penal Code 995 was proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant attorney's conviction for solicitation of a bribe because defendant had requisite intent to bribe when the solicitation of a police officer in his official capacity was made as supported by corroborating testimony of two witnesses. Moreover, the denial of a motion to quash indictment was proper because defendant's privilege against self-incrimination was not violated, and probable cause supported the indictment.

 

611 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Wisdom


Crim. No. 6845


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division One


47 Cal. App. 3d 482; 120 Cal. Rptr. 745; 1975 Cal. App. LEXIS 1040



April 24, 1975 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's petition for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied June 19, 1975.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of San Diego County, Nos. CR-28988, CR-30959, William T. Low, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgments are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review from judgments of imprisonment, under Cal. Penal. Code. § 3053, and for convictions of robbery in the second degree and attempted burglary entered in the Superior Court of San Diego County (California). Appellant contended that § 3053 was unconstitutional because it conferred allowed the director of corrections the authority to veto a court decision.


OVERVIEW: Appellant had been convicted of robbery in the second degree and attempted burglary. Imposition of sentence in each case had been suspended so that appellant could file petitions pursuant to Cal. Welf. & Inst. § 3051 to determine whether appellant should have been committed for detention, treatment, and rehabilitation in the narcotics facility. Appellant was committed and ultimately the corrections authorities determined that appellant was unsuitable for retention and returned him to the trial court for further proceedings. The trial court then conducted a hearing and concluded that appellant should be and did sentence him to imprisonment. The court affirmed the judgments of sentence because the decision of the correction authorities was not an administrative decision and not a judicial decision. The court pointed out that the trial court determined whether appellant should have been committed to the narcotics facility. This decision allowed the corrections authorities to determine whether appellant was a fit subject for rehabilitation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgments of imprisonment because the decision of the correction authority to return him to the trial court for further proceedings was an administrative decision and not a judicial decision.

 

612 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


City of Downey v. Board of Administration


Civ. No. 44526


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Four


47 Cal. App. 3d 621; 121 Cal. Rptr. 295; 1975 Cal. App. LEXIS 1052



April 24, 1975 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellants' petition for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied June 19, 1975.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. C14769, Stevens Fargo, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, cities and city employees, sought review of the judgment from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), that found amendments to the Public Employees Retirement Law, Cal. Gov't Code §§ 20000 (1971), did not violate Cal. Const. art. XI, § 5, and did not infringe upon the home rule provisions under Cal. Const. art. XVI, § 6.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, cities and city employees, instituted litigation against respondent Board of Administration because the amendments to the Public Employees' Retirement Law, Cal. Gov't Code § 20000 (1971) violated Cal. Const. art. XVI, § 6, and infringed upon the home rule provisions under Cal. Const. art. XI, § 5. The trial court found against appellants' contentions and appellants sought review. The appellate court found that the amendments that merged the retirement accounts of contributing agencies into a single account did not violate art. XVI, § 6. Further, the appellate court found that the amendments had built-in safeguards. The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment because the amendments were constitutional as that they did not give or lend the credit of appellant cities to other contracting agencies, and did not conflict with local regulation nor involve a question of preemption and as such, did not infringe upon the home rule provisions.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment because the amendments to the Public Employees' Retirement Law were constitutional as that they did not give or lend the credit of appellant cities to other contracting agencies, and did not conflict with local regulation nor involve a question of preemption and as such, did not infringe upon the home rule provisions.

 

613 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Kirby v. Alcoholic Bev. Etc. Appeals Bd.


Civ. No. 35804


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Two


47 Cal. App. 3d 360; 120 Cal. Rptr. 847; 1975 Cal. App. LEXIS 1027



April 22, 1975 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petitions for a rehearing were denied May 22, 1975, and the petitions of the respondent and the real parties in interest for a hearing by the Supreme Court were denied June 19, 1975.



DISPOSITION: The decisions of the board are annulled. The board is directed to reinstate the orders of the department.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner licensees sought review of decisions by the Alcoholic Beverage Control Appeals Board (California), which reversed three orders of the Department of Alcoholic Beverage Control suspending on-sale liquor licenses of petitioners for violations of Cal. Code Regs. tit. 4, § 143.3, that met the provisions of Cal. Const. art. XX, § 22, and Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 24200(a) and (b).


OVERVIEW: Petitioner licensees' licenses to sell liquor were suspended by the Department of Alcoholic Beverages Control (Department) because they repeatedly violated Cal. Code Regs. tit. 4, § 143.3 by allowing simulated sex acts in their establishments when serving alcohol. The department determined that the violations were sufficient to establish grounds for suspension or revocation of the licenses pursuant to Cal. Const. art. XX, § 22, and Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 24200(a) and (b). The court annulled the decisions of the Alcoholic Beverage Control Appeals Board (Board) that reversed the department's suspensions, finding that there was no conflict between § 143.3 and Cal. Penal Code §§ 318.5 and 318.6. The court reasoned that local ordinances adopted pursuant to §§ 318.5 and 318.6 were penal in nature and merely permitted cities to proscribe the state of undress of employees in establishments that served food and beverages, and that was distinct from the department's jurisdiction to license and regulate all aspects of alcoholic beverages. Thus the court concluded that there was no issue of preemption involved when the department pursuant to article XX, § 22, promulgated § 143.3.


OUTCOME: The decisions of the Alcoholic Beverage Control Appeals Board reversing orders suspending petitioner licensees' on-sale liquor licenses were annulled. The Department of Alcoholic Beverage Control, pursuant its constitutional authority to regulate the sale of drinks in premises it licensed, could promulgate a rule prohibiting simulated sex acts in those liquor establishments without conflicting with the California Penal Code.

 

614 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Journey v. Superior Court


Civ. No. 14296


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division One


47 Cal. App. 3d 408; 120 Cal. Rptr. 897; 1975 Cal. App. LEXIS 1032



April 22, 1975 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A petition for a rehearing was denied May 8, 1975, and respondent's petition for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied June 19, 1975.



DISPOSITION: Let a writ of mandate issue commanding the criminal presiding department of the San Diego County Superior Court to grant petitioner's motion under Code of Civil Procedure section 170.6 for an order reassigning the cause to another and different judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought a writ of prohibition and/or mandate to compel respondent judge to disqualify himself under the provisions of Cal. Code Civ. Proc. § 170.6 and for an order transferring his cause to another judge of the San Diego County Superior Court.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner appeared before the judge on a probation revocation hearing and timely filed a court-provided form entitled "Declaration of Prejudice (170.6 C.C.P.)," which substantially complied with the provisions of § 170.6. The judge denied his motion for an order reassigning the case to another judge, claiming that no facts were stated in the motion and because § 170.6, as applied to that criminal proceeding, was unconstitutional. Petitioner then sought a writ to compel his case to be transferred to another judge. The court issued a writ of mandate to grant petitioner's motion. It held that the judge's contention that the declaration should state facts was unmeritorious, as proof of facts showing actual prejudice was not required and, to the contrary, the right to disqualify a judge was automatic in the sense that a good faith belief in the judge's prejudice alone was sufficient. Further, when the affidavit was timely and properly made, immediate disqualification was mandatory and the court was bound to accept proper affidavits without further inquiry. The court also held that §170.6 was not an unwarranted interference with the constitutional and orderly processes of the court.


OUTCOME: The court granted petitioner a writ of mandate commanding the criminal presiding department of the San Diego County Superior Court to grant petitioner's motion for an order reassigning the cause to another and different judge.

 

615 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Rodgers


Crim. No. 6910


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division One


47 Cal. App. 3d 992; 121 Cal. Rptr. 346; 1975 Cal. App. LEXIS 1084



April 22, 1975 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of San Diego County, No. CR-31572, Jack R. Levitt, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Superior Court of San Diego County (California) convicting him of transporting marijuana in violation of Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11360 and possessing marijuana for sale in violation of Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11359.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with transporting marijuana in violation of Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11360 and possessing marijuana for sale in violation of Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11359. Defendant filed a notice of a motion to suppress under Cal. Penal Code § 1538.5, and the motion was set for hearing. Defense counsel filed a motion to transfer the hearing to another court under Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 170.6 on the grounds that he believed the trial court judge was prejudiced against defendant's interest so that he could not have a fair and impartial hearing before him. The trial court required counsel to testify to facts supporting his conclusion. The trial court denied the motion. After a subsequent trial, defendant was convicted on both counts. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment. The court held that the motion to transfer should have been granted. The court ruled that a defendant's right to a transfer was automatic insofar as a good faith belief in a trial court's prejudice was the only requisite. Thus, the court ruled that proof of facts was unnecessary. Because the affidavit was timely and properly made, the court ruled that immediate disqualification was mandatory.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment convicting defendant of transporting marijuana and possessing marijuana for sale.

 

616 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Katz


Crim. No. 25710


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


47 Cal. App. 3d 294; 120 Cal. Rptr. 603; 1975 Cal. App. LEXIS 1022



April 17, 1975 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. A301550, Billy G. Mills, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant second-hand dealer appealed a conviction from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) for receiving stolen property in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 496.


OVERVIEW: Defendant second-hand dealer, during his trial for receiving stolen property, under Cal. Penal Code § 496, was required to show pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 496(2), (3) and Cal. Jury Instructions Criminal No. 14.66 that he made a reasonable inquiry into the source of property he received from a third person. Defendant was convicted, and he appealed. Defendant's conviction was affirmed because § 496(2), (3) the rebuttal presumption, that defendant's failure to make reasonable inquiry proved knowledge that the property was stolen, did not eliminate prosecution's burden to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that the property was stolen and that the circumstances of receiving the property warranted defendant making a reasonable inquiry. Further, the particular instruction to the jury clearly expressed the reasonable doubt standard and any affirmative defense provided for by § 496(3). Moreover where no fundamental right or suspect classification was involved, equal protection was not violated by a categorization that required those, who handled easily fenced goods, to make inquiry of the goods' title and origin if the circumstances of receipt were suspicious.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant second-hand dealer's conviction for receiving stolen goods because there was no unconstitutional shift of the burden of proof from the prosecution to defendant, presumptions in criminal cases were constitutional, and there was no equal protection violation when defendant was statutorily required to inquire as to the title and origin of second-hand goods.

 

617 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Malone v. Superior Court


Civ. No. 14888


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


47 Cal. App. 3d 313; 120 Cal. Rptr. 851; 1975 Cal. App. LEXIS 1024



April 17, 1975 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A petition for a rehearing was denied May 5, 1975, and the petition of the real party in interest for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied June 26, 1975. Richardson, J., did not participate therein.



DISPOSITION: Let a writ of prohibition issue as prayed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner filed a writ of prohibition with the court that sought to prevent further proceedings by the people, the real party in interest, in respondent magistrate court upon an indictment that charged petitioner with receiving stolen property and three prior felony convictions because respondent reduced petitioner's charges to misdemeanors pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 17(b)(5).


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was charged with burglary and receiving stolen goods. At a preliminary hearing the people, the real party in interest, and petitioner stipulated that both charges would be tried as misdemeanors. New information prompted the people to file a second complaint for a felony indictment. The grand jury returned an indictment that charged petitioner with receipt of stolen goods and three prior felony convictions. After the indictment, respondent magistrate court dismissed the complaint in furtherance of justice at the people's request. Respondent reduced petitioner's charges to misdemeanors upon the consent of the parties pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 17(b)(5). Petitioner then sought a writ of prohibition to prevent further proceedings upon the felony indictment. The court granted the writ of prohibition. The court held that respondent had dismissed the felony complaint and fixed the offense as a misdemeanor under § 17(b)(5). Respondent did not consent to the abrogation of the judicial act whereby the offenses were classified as misdemeanors. The character of the charges as misdemeanors persisted and dismissal of the complaint barred further felony prosecution.


OUTCOME: The court issued a writ of prohibition that prevented further proceedings by the people, real party in interest, against petitioner in respondent magistrate court upon an indictment that charged petitioner with receiving stolen property and three prior felony convictions because respondent dismissed the complaint, fixed the offense as a misdemeanor, and did not consent to further prosecution on the felony indictment.

 

618 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Perrine


Crim. No. 26146


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Four


47 Cal. App. 3d 252; 120 Cal. Rptr. 640; 1975 Cal. App. LEXIS 1018



April 16, 1975 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petitions for a rehearing were denied May 6, 1975, and respondents' petitions for a hearing by the Supreme Court were denied June 11, 1975.


PRIOR HISTORY: Municipal Court for the East Los Angeles Judicial District of Los Angeles County, Nos. M147997, M148139, M149540, M149542, M152532 and M148138, Robert M. Takasugi, Judge.



DISPOSITION: In each case, the order dismissing the complaint is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The prosecution appealed the order of the Municipal Court for the East Los Angeles Judicial District of Los Angeles County (California), which granted defendant unlicensed picture arcade managers' motion to dismiss on the ground that Los Angeles, Cal., County Ordinance 5860, § 2732, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: In consolidated cases, defendant unlicensed picture arcade managers were charged with operating a picture arcade without a licensed manager being present in violation of Los Angeles, Cal., County Ordinance 5860, § 2732, and with acting as a manager of a picture arcade without a license. The trial court granted defendants' motion to dismiss upon the ground that the ordinance was so vague and uncertain as to be unconstitutional, and the prosecution appealed. The court reversed the dismissal of the charges because the court found that "responsible" as used in the ordinance was a description of a job function, which was fair and reasonable under U.S. Const. amend. I. The ordinance did not restrict defendants' U.S. Const. amend. I rights but was the constitutional exercise of county police powers to prevent dangerous and unlawful conduct which would be anticipated in an unattended picture arcade.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order that granted defendant unlicensed picture arcade managers' motion to dismiss charges of operating a picture arcade without a licensed manager being present and acting as a manager of a picture arcade without a license. The court found that the ordinance was not unconstitutionally vague nor did it place restrictions on defendants' First Amendment Freedom of Speech rights, thus, the ordinance was constitutional.

 

619 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Smock v. Carleson


Civ. No. 35191


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Three


47 Cal. App. 3d 960; 121 Cal. Rptr. 432; 1975 Cal. App. LEXIS 1081



April 15, 1975 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Alameda County, No. 432978, Lionel J. Wilson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the director of the department of social welfare and secretary of the health and welfare agency of California, challenged the writ of mandate of the Superior Court of Alameda County (California), which enjoined enforcement of the Eligibility and Assistance Standards § 44-213.4 and ordered appellants to return money withheld from the date that respondent recipients applied for Aid to Families with Dependent Children.


OVERVIEW: The trial court entered a writ of mandate ordering appellants, the director of the department of social welfare and secretary of the health and welfare agency of California, to return money withheld pursuant to the Eligibility and Assistance Standards § 44-213.4 from the date respondent recipients applied for assistance. The trial court enjoined appellants from enforcing the regulations to the extent that they resulted in the exclusion of needy natural parents, residing with their eligible children, from the budget unit used to compute grants for Aid to Families with Dependent Children. Appellants sought review. The court affirmed because the classification of different living styles so that a family with deprived children received a lower grant solely because the parents were unmarried violated the equal protection clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV and conflicted with Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 11250. The court held that fostering the favored family concept did not furnish a substantial justification for different treatment based on marital status. The court found that the trial court correctly ordered payment of benefits to be retroactive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the writ of mandate ordering retroactive payments of AFDC benefits to respondent recipients, because appellants, the director of the department of social welfare and secretary of the health and welfare agency of California, had no reasonable justification for enforcing regulations that benefitted the deprived children of unmarried parents to a lesser extent than the deprived children of married parents.

Southern Cal. Assn. of Seventh-Day Adventists v. Franchise Tax Bd.


Civ. No. 44077


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Five


47 Cal. App. 3d 207; 120 Cal. Rptr. 622; 1975 Cal. App. LEXIS 1012



April 15, 1975 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. C-62755, James D. Tante, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the California Franchise Tax Board, challenged a judgment in favor of respondent religious/educational association by the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) in an action for refund of franchise taxes paid by respondent after appellant revoked respondent's religious/educational exemption from the franchise tax pursuant to Cal. Rev. & Tax. Code § 23704.5, which the superior court held unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Respondent religious/educational association brought an action for refund of franchise taxes it paid after appellant, the California Franchise Tax Board, revoked respondent's tax exemption pursuant to Cal. Rev. & Tax. Code § 23704.5. Appellant revoked the exemption due to respondent's operation through its parochial school of a coin laundry that provided service to the public for compensation. The trial court ruled that § 23704.5 was unconstitutional. The court agreed on appeal, finding that § 23704.5 created an arbitrary and capricious classification singling out religious/educational organizations that operated laundry facilities from other nonprofits and other types of business, and denied respondent equal protection of the law because other categories of exempt nonprofit organizations were not similarly precluded from engaging in profit-making commercial ventures. The court found that any competitive advantage from the franchise tax exemption for nonprofit organizations had been corrected by the adoption of an unrelated business income tax, and that the purpose for enactment of § 23704.5, backed by a laundry and linen supply association, was suspect.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court's judgment, holding that the statute requiring revocation of respondent religious/educational association's franchise tax exemption due to its provision of laundry services to the public was unconstitutional. The statute created an arbitrary and discriminatory classification that unfairly deprived respondent of a tax exemption while others similarly situated could engage in the same business without penalty.

 

621 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Keogh


Crim. No. 24253


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Four


46 Cal. App. 3d 919; 120 Cal. Rptr. 817; 1975 Cal. App. LEXIS 1820



April 8, 1975 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Respondent's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied June 4, 1975. Clark, J., was of the Opinion that the Petition should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. A-432151, John L. Donnellan and Julius A. Leetham, Judges.



DISPOSITION: Judgment as to count VI is reversed. Judgment as to counts II, III, IV and V is affirmed, but the sentence is hereby set aside and the matter remanded for resentencing in light of the views expressed in this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction by the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) of forgery and of receiving stolen property. Defendant contended that the trial court judge erred in refusing to suppress certain evidence obtained by police officers who arrested defendant. Defendant also contended that sentence imposed for forgery constituted cruel and unusual punishment, prohibited by Cal. Const. art. I, § 6.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted by the trial court of receiving stolen property and of four counts of forgery. The sentences on the four counts of forgery were ordered to run consecutively to each other. The sentence on receiving of stolen property conviction was ordered to run concurrently with the sentences on the forgery convictions. The court reversed the trial court. The court held that the trial judge erred in refusing to suppress certain evidence obtained by police officers who arrested defendant. The court reasoned that the officers did not announce their identities or their purpose while standing outside defendant's apartment, as they were required to do by Cal. Penal Code §§ 844, 1531. The court held that the trial court's error necessitated the reversal of defendant's conviction of receiving stolen property. It reasoned that without the evidence that should have been suppressed, there was no substantial evidence to support the conviction. The court also held that a life sentence for forgery of checks in an aggregate amount of less than $ 500 constituted cruel or unusual punishment, prohibited by Cal. Const. art. I, § 6.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's conviction of defendant of receiving stolen property, affirmed defendant's conviction of four counts of forgery, and remanded the matter for resentencing. The court did so because without the evidence that the trial court should have suppressed, there was no substantial evidence to support the conviction of receiving stolen property and because the forgery sentence constituted cruel and unusual punishment.

 

622 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Fallen Leaf Protection Asso. v. State


Civ. No. 14827


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


46 Cal. App. 3d 816; 120 Cal. Rptr. 538; 1975 Cal. App. LEXIS 1814



April 3, 1975 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied April 21, 1975, and Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied May 28, 1975.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of El Dorado County, No. 22677, Charles F. Fogerty, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of dismissal is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners sought review of a decision by the Superior Court of El Dorado County (California), which granted defendant state's demurrer in response to plaintiffs' cross-complaint for inverse condemnation. Plaintiffs contended that Cal. Water Code §§ 13950- 13951 under which defendant sought inverse condemnation of plaintiffs' cesspools and septic tanks, were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff property owners brought a cross-complaint against defendant state for inverse condemnation of plaintiffs' septic tanks and cesspools. The trial court sustained defendant's general demurrer without leave to amend on the grounds that no cause of action had been stated for the reason that direction to comply with Cal. Water Code § 13951 was a valid exercise of defendant's police power. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment of dismissal. The court held that police power was one of the most essential powers of government and one that was least limitable. Thus, even though plaintiffs' cesspools and septic tanks might not be a nuisance per se, it was still within the police power to declare them a nuisance for regulatory purposes. The court held that Cal. Water Code § 13950 was not arbitrary as applied, even though in defendant's cross-complaint there was no claim that plaintiffs' existing waste disposal systems constituted a nuisance in fact. The court reasoned that § 13950 expressly declared the disposal systems to be a nuisance; hence, no such claim was required.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's dismissal of plaintiff property owners' cross-complaint against defendant state for inverse condemnation. The court did so because it found that the statutes under which defendant sought inverse condemnation of plaintiffs' cesspools and septic tanks were not unconstitutional but a valid statement of defendant's police power.

 

623 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


E. M. Consumer Corp. v. Christensen


Civ. No. 33436


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Two


47 Cal. App. 3d 642; 121 Cal. Rptr. 177; 1975 Cal. App. LEXIS 1054



April 1, 1975 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Santa Clara County, No. 281241, George H. Barnett, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant consumer corporation challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of Santa Clara County (California), denying their petition for writ of mandate and declaring that the minimum price order of respondent Director of Agriculture of the State of California was constitutional and valid. Appellant contended that in setting the minimum price several economic factors were not considered and that the proceedings were procedurally defective.


OVERVIEW: Respondent Director of Agriculture of the State of California held a public hearing to review the minimum prices of milk sold in one gallon containers in specific markets. Subsequently, respondent determined that a price increase for milk sold in one gallon plastic containers was justified. Appellant consumer corporation requested that the minimum price order be set aside. The trial court denied the request. Appellant filed a petition for writ of mandate seeking to set aside the price order contending that in setting the minimum price, respondent failed to consider several economic factors and that the proceedings were defective. The court denied the petition and affirmed the trial court's decision. The court held that respondent need not have considered the production cost of half gallon plastic containers where type of container was not a "method of distribution," the minimum price was properly based on the predominant container in which milk was sold, and consumer purchase power and available capacity were correctly considered at a prior hearing. The court held that appellant was properly restricted from conducting cross-examination and from introducing evidence at trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment denying appellant consumer corporation's petition for writ of mandate and declaring that the minimum price order of respondent Director of Agriculture of the State of California was constitutional and valid. The court held that in setting the minimum price respondent properly considered applicable economic factors and that the administrative hearing and trial below were not procedurally defective.

 

624 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Martinez


Crim. Nos. 7680, 7746


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


46 Cal. App. 3d 736; 120 Cal. Rptr. 362; 121 Cal. Rptr. 443; 1975 Cal. App. LEXIS 1806



March 31, 1975 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied 46 Cal. App. 3d 736 at 746.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Placer County, Nos. 41393, 38815, Leland J. Propp, Judge.



DISPOSITION: In 3 Crim. 7746 (Placer County Superior Court No. 38815) the order revoking probation is reversed, with directions to the superior court to enter an order vacating the judgment and to furnish the Department of Corrections with a certified copy of that order. In 3 Crim. 7680 (Placer County Superior Court No. 41393) the judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the order of the Superior Court of Placer County (California), which revoked his probation under Cal. Penal Code § 1203.2a, after he was convicted and confined for violating Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11377. Defendant signed a waiver of his right to appear at the revocation hearing. Defendant was represented by the public defender. Defendant also appealed his guilty plea in the § 11377 conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty, was given probation, and then had his probation revoked after waiving his right to be present at the hearing. On appeal, the court consolidated defendant's appeals, reversed the probation revocation order, and affirmed defendant's conviction for possession of barbiturates, Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11377. The court held that the revocation order was void. Defendant's waiver was not authorized by Cal. Penal Code § 1203.2a, because the trial court's jurisdiction to revoke defendant's probation expired 30 days after the court was notified that defendant had been convicted and confined for a second offense. Also, the waiver did not purport to waive the 30-day time period. The court heard defendant's appeal from his guilty plea notwithstanding defendant's failure to seek a certificate of probable cause as required by Cal. Penal Code § 1237.5, because the trial judge effectively certified the case for appeal when he directed the transcript to be prepared. The court found that a subsequent revocation of probation was a "collateral" rather than a "direct" consequence of the guilty plea, and defendant need not be advised of such consequences.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the probation revocation order. Waiver was not authorized, the trial court's jurisdiction to revoke defendant's probation based on a subsequent conviction had expired, and defendant did not waive the 30-day time period. Defendant's conviction of possession of barbiturates was affirmed. Defendant understood that the prior conviction increased his sentence and did not have to be told about collateral consequences of his plea.

People v. Mackey


Crim. No. 6949


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division One


46 Cal. App. 3d 755; 120 Cal. Rptr. 157; 1975 Cal. App. LEXIS 1808



March 31, 1975 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied May 28, 1975.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of San Diego County, No. CR-31547, Paul E. Overton, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the Superior Court of San Diego County (California), which convicted defendant of unlawful sexual intercourse with a female under the age of 18 under Cal. Penal Code § 261.5, and committed him to the youth authority. Defendant asserted that the trial court exceeded its jurisdiction with his sentence and that § 261.5 was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of unlawful sexual intercourse with a female under the age of 18 under Cal. Penal Code § 261.5, and the jury recommended he be punished by confinement in the county jail. The trial court committed defendant to the youth authority. On appeal defendant asserted that the trial court exceeded its jurisdiction by not following the jury's recommendation and that § 261.5, was unconstitutional because it only protected females and not males from unwanted sexual intercourse. On review the court held that the trial court could commit defendant to the youth authority under Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 1731.5. The court held that it was unrealistic to base a conclusion on the reasonableness of § 261.5, classification of the protected class upon a belief that girls of 14, the same age as the victim, were no more likely than boys of the same age to be the objects of the desires and designs of older people of the opposite sex who are on the prowl. The court held that the statute was not unconstitutional in extending its protection to only females under the age of 18 and affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for unlawful sexual intercourse with a female under the age of 18 and his commitment to the youth authority. The trial court had jurisdiction to commit defendant to the youth authority and the statute he was convicted under was not unconstitutional in its protected class being only females and not males.

In re Wells


Crim. No. 26286


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


46 Cal. App. 3d 592; 121 Cal. Rptr. 23; 1975 Cal. App. LEXIS 1795



March 28, 1975 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Respondent's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied June 11, 1975. Clark, J., was of the Opinion that the Petition should be Granted.



DISPOSITION: The writ is granted and petitioner is ordered discharged from custody.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought habeas corpus relief from the imposition of a 20 year sentence on a conviction pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 647(a) on the grounds that the sentence was cruel and unusual punishment under Cal. Const. art. I, § 6.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was convicted of annoying or molesting a child pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 647(a), a misdemeanor, but because of a prior conviction for lewd and lascivious acts with a child under Cal. Penal Code § 288 was exposed to possible life imprisonment by the recidivist provision of § 647(a). The court found that petitioner had standing to challenge § 647(a) because although he was on probation he was still in constructive custody and although his sentence had been fixed at twenty years his sentence could be redetermined before his final discharge. The court also found that the penalty imposed by the recidivist portion of § 647(a) was unconstitutionally cruel and unusual because the penalty was disproportionate when compared with the punishment prescribed for more serious offenses and no other state imposed so harsh a penalty for this type of crime. The court granted petitioner's request for habeas corpus relief and freed him from all custody, actual or constructive, because of the extensive time he had already spent in prison.


OUTCOME: The court granted petitioner's request for habeas corpus relief because the penalty imposed upon him for violation of the child molestation statute was disproportionate when compared with the punishment prescribed for more serious offenses and no other state imposed so harsh a penalty for this type of crime.

Phillips v. Bartolomie


Civ. No. 32849


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Two


46 Cal. App. 3d 346; 121 Cal. Rptr. 56; 1975 Cal. App. LEXIS 1779



March 24, 1975 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied May 22, 1975.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Mendocino County, No. 32795, Arthur B. Broaddus, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of dismissal is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant debtors sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of Mendocino County (California), which dismissed appellants' actions for injunctive and declaratory relief against respondents, sheriff and creditor, that arose over attempts by respondents to garnish appellants' bank accounts.


OVERVIEW: Respondent sheriff garnished appellant debtors' bank account without first notifying appellants, in an attempt to satisfy a money judgment in favor of respondent creditor. Appellants claimed that the money in the account came from federal disability benefits that were exempt from garnishment by federal law. The court affirmed the dismissal of appellants' actions and found that Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 690.18, which required judgment debtors to apply for and prove a right to an exemption, was not an unreasonable burden and therefore the failure of respondent sheriff to give appellants notice before garnishing the account was not a violation of due process. Furthermore, the court found that § 690.18 was not preempted by federal statutes that exempted federal benefits from garnishment because there was no conflict between the federal and state laws and there was nothing to bar the state from requiring the debtor apply for an exemption first.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of appellant debtors' action for injunctive and declaratory relief against respondents, sheriff and creditor, because the state statutes requiring a debtor to apply for an exemption to keep money received from federal disability benefits from being garnished did not violate due process and were not preempted by federal law.

DISPOSITION: For these reasons we hold that it was not impossible, impracticable or futile for the senior Lopas to have filed their action against Lopa, Jr., and hence to have served and returned summons, at an earlier date. It follows that the motion to dismiss was erroneously denied. A peremptory writ of mandate will issue commanding respondent to vacate its denial of the motion to dismiss and to grant the motion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner tortfeasor sought review of the orders of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which denied petitioner's motions to quash service of summons and to dismiss the underlying suit against him under Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 581a.

Code § 474, the trial court properly allowed respondents to amend because at the time they filed their original complaint, respondents were unaware that they had a cause of action against petitioner. The motion to dismiss should have been granted because the statute of limitations, under Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 581a, to serve a summons had run and was not tolled by the existence of contrary precedent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of petitioner tortfeasor's motion to quash service because respondents parents of decedent were unaware they had a cause of action against petitioner. The court reversed the denial the motion to dismiss because the statute of limitations for service of the service of summons had run.

Frost v. Trustees of Cal. State University and Colleges


Civ. No. 35557


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Three


46 Cal. App. 3d 225; 120 Cal. Rptr. 1; 1975 Cal. App. LEXIS 1768



March 19, 1975 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied April 18, 1975, and the Opinion was Modified to Read as Printed Above. Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied May 14, 1975.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco, No. 648970, Ira A. Brown, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner probationary employee appealed from a judgment entered in the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California) which denied his petition for writ of mandamus to compel payment of accrued back salary, against respondents, university trustees, State Board of Control, State Personnel Board, and State Controller. Petitioner claimed he was entitled to pay for periods he did not work and to the cost of a transcript.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner probationary employee sought a writ of mandamus to compel payment of back pay against respondents, university trustees, State Board of Control, State Personnel Board, and State Controller. At the end of an academic year petitioner was not invited to return. Petitioner followed a grievance and appeal procedure and was ultimately invited to return. Petitioner claimed that he was due pay for the period he was not working. The court affirmed the decision of the trial court and determined that petitioner was not eligible for pay for the period of time he did not work. The court found that this was not a wrongful dismissal case, but merely a decision not to renew petitioner's annual appointment. The court ruled that it was not required that probationary academic employees who were notified that they would not be rehired, and who thereafter were in fact rehired, be paid for the interim period during which they did not work. The court denied petitioner's request for the cost of the transcript prepared for his grievance procedure.


OUTCOME: The court ruled that petitioner probationary employee was ineligible for pay for the time he was not employed by respondents, university trustees, State Board of Control, State Personnel Board, and State Controller. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court and denied petitioner's request for costs.

People v. Schrieber


Crim. No. 7831


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


45 Cal. App. 3d 917; 119 Cal. Rptr. 812; 1975 Cal. App. LEXIS 1739



March 11, 1975 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied May 8, 1975.


PRIOR HISTORY: Justice Court for the Redding Judicial District of Shasta County, No. 73T188, Joseph Bertagna, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment from the justice court convicting him of driving while under the influence of intoxicating liquor in violation of Cal. Veh. Code § 23102(a). The Superior Court of Shasta County (California) reversed the justice court's decision to convict defendant and certified the case to the court.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted in the justice court of driving while under the influence of intoxicating liquor under Cal. Veh. Code § 23102(a). The superior court reversed defendant's conviction because it found Cal. Veh. Code § 23126 unconstitutional. On further appeal, the court affirmed defendant's conviction. The court held that there was a rational connection between the blood alcohol level at the time of defendant's arrest and the taking of the blood alcohol test, even with an absence of a time limit between the two events. The rebuttable presumption that defendant was inebriated with a blood alcohol level of .10 percent did not make the statute unconstitutional because defendant could have introduced evidence that he was not inebriated and the state was still required to prove its burden beyond a reasonable doubt. Also, the objective determination of inebriation was a more satisfactory means to prove inebriation rather than subjective observations. Pursuant to court precedent on other statutes which created a presumption, § 23102 was not unconstitutional under U.S. Const. amend. V because defendant had the duty to explain the blood alcohol level.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the superior court's decision and affirmed defendant's conviction of driving while under the influence of intoxicating liquor. There was a rational connection between defendant's blood alcohol level at the time of the offense and at the time of the blood alcohol test, and defendant was not deprived of the presumption of innocence by the rebuttable presumption of the blood alcohol level which established the offense.

 

633 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Gawzner Corp. v. Minier


Civ. No. 44362


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


46 Cal. App. 3d 777; 120 Cal. Rptr. 344; 1975 Cal. App. LEXIS 1811; 80 A.L.R.3d 726



March 11, 1975 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Santa Barbara County, No. 91921, Richard C. Kirkpatrick, Judge. *


* Assigned by the Chairman of the Judicial Council.



DISPOSITION: The order denying defendant's motion to dissolve the permanent injunction is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant district attorney appealed the order of the Superior Court of Santa Barbara County (California), which denied defendant's motion to dissolve the permanent injunction that prohibited him from enforcing Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 17564 pertaining to outside advertising against plaintiff hotels.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff hotels filed an action to enjoin defendant district attorney from enforcing against them the provisions of Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 17564, which prohibited certain room rate advertising. The lower court granted the permanent injunction after determining that § 17564 applied to motels and not hotels, and therefore was an invalid exercise of police power and violated the Equal Protection Clause, U.S. Const. amend. XIV. The court affirmed the injunction, noting that it must defer to the lower court's discretion in determining that an injunction was necessary and holding that the issuance of the Attorney General's opinion was not a change in circumstance sufficient to justify the dissolution of the injunction. The court looked to the plain meaning of the applicable Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code statutes and determined that hotels did not fall within the classification of § 17564. Consequently, the legislature was discriminating against motels by limiting their ability to advertise when they were similarly situated to hotels. Accordingly, the statute was held to be unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order denying defendant district attorney's motion to dissolve the permanent injunction, holding that, because the statute prohibiting room rate outside advertising by motels differentiated between hotel and motel advertisement in an unreasonable manner, it violated the Equal Protection Clause and was, therefore, not enforceable.

 

634 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Solander v. Municipal Court for Sacramento Judicial Dist.


Civ. No. 14172


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


45 Cal. App. 3d 664; 119 Cal. Rptr. 609; 1975 Cal. App. LEXIS 1719



March 3, 1975 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The Petition of the Plaintiff and Respondent for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied May 1, 1975. Richardson, J. did not Participate therein.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Sacramento County, No. 229450, Mamoru Sakuma, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The award of costs is annulled, the judgment issuing the writ of prohibition is reversed, and the writ is ordered discharged.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The people sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of Sacramento County (California), which entered judgment granting a writ prohibiting further prosecution of a criminal complaint against defendant that alleged violations of the Sacramento City Code § 17.7 and of Cal. Health & Safety Code § 28546, both relating to restaurant sanitation.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with violating Sacramento City Code § 17.7 and Cal. Health & Safety Code § 28546, both of which imposed penalties relating to restaurant sanitation. The lower court determined that the term "accessible" as used in the city ordinance and the phrase "provided in all areas" as used in § 28546 were so vague by definition and application that each section was void. Reversing that decision on appeal, the court held that term "provided" simply meant, "supplied." The court applied the reasonable certainty test to § 28546 and concluded that the statute was sufficiently certain to accord with constitutional due process standards. The court therefore found no unconstitutional vagueness emanating from the use of the words "provided in all areas" as contained in § 28546 nor in the use of the phrase "accessible to all rooms" as contained in the city ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment issuing the writ of prohibition, and therefore discharged the writ because defendant's due process rights were not violated as the statutes he was charged with violating concerning restaurant sanitation were not unconstitutionally vague.

 

635 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


In re Contreras


Crim. No. 2165


Court of Appeal of California, Fifth Appellate District


45 Cal. App. 3d 549; 119 Cal. Rptr. 757; 1975 Cal. App. LEXIS 1707



February 25, 1975 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Let a writ of habeas corpus issue directing the Department of Corrections to modify its designation of petitioner's termer status in his prison record in accordance with the views expressed herein; relief is otherwise denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate sought a writ of habeas corpus challenging a judgment of the San Diego Superior Court (California), which denied petitioner probation for his conviction of possession of heroin and sentenced petitioner to state prison.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner inmate sought a writ of habeas corpus after probation was denied and he was sentenced to prison. Petitioner challenged the designation of his status in the records of the corrections department and the use of two prior convictions in the sentencing proceedings. The court granted the petition as to the designation of his status in the corrections department records because although the department was authorized to maintain a complete record of an inmate's personal and social history, indicating the inmate's status with the simple appellation "third term," "second term," without accompanying such designation with all pertinent information surrounding any conviction, including all subsequent dispositions, was invalid because such a designation harbored a great potential for misuse in the granting of an earlier discretionary parole date. The use of the probation report containing petitioner's prior convictions at the sentencing hearing did not warrant a new sentencing hearing because the court considered and rejected probation as an act of informed discretion, on its merits, and in so doing was not acting upon misinformation as to the validity of a prior conviction.


OUTCOME: The court granted petitioner inmate's writ of habeas corpus as to the designation of his term status in his prison record because such designation was invalid as it harbored a great potential for misuse in the granting of an earlier discretionary parole date. The court denied the writ as to the use of petitioner's probation report at his sentencing hearing because the trial court considered and rejected probation on its merits.

 

636 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


James v. Municipal Court for Camarillo Judicial Dist.


Civ. No. 44044


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


45 Cal. App. 3d 557; 119 Cal. Rptr. 606; 1975 Cal. App. LEXIS 1708



February 25, 1975 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied May 1, 1975.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Ventura County, No. SP-47123, Richard C. Heaton, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The order is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order of respondent Superior Court of Ventura County (California), which denied his petition for a writ of prohibition and mandamus which sought to declare unconstitutional his conviction for driving under the influence of intoxicating liquor.


OVERVIEW: In a mass arraignment in respondent court, defendant pled guilty to driving under the influence of intoxicating liquor. The docket sheet showed that defendant was advised of all of his rights. The reporter's transcript indicated that the trial judge, when defendant's attempted to plead guilty without benefit of counsel, reiterated advice regarding defendant's right to counsel. A few months later, defendant was charged with a second violation of the same statute, and his probation was revoked. Defendant sought a writ of prohibition and mandamus seeking to have the prior conviction declared unconstitutional because he was not properly advised of his right to have counsel appointed if he could not afford counsel. The superior court denied the writ. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that facts did not support defendant's contention. The court noted that defendant did not allege that he was indigent at the time of trial. The court found that the reporter's transcript indicated that, when defendant appeared before the court a deputy public defender was present with him, the court twice asked defendant if he desired an attorney and only then accepted the plea.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of the writ, rejecting defendant's argument that the conviction was unconstitutional because he was not advised of his right to appointed counsel if he could not afford one. The court held that the docket sheet showed that defendant was properly advised his rights, the record reflected that respondent court specifically advised defendant of his right to counsel, and there was no proof that defendant was indigent.
